{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01HLNhxG1WRFKa6WAyLoNSeV","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I can see the issue more clearly:\n\n1. At line 880-886, when a command succeeds, rirb_error is reset to 0 and poll_count is reset to 0 (if not in forced polling mode)\n2. At line 882, rirb_error is reset to 0 when a response is received\n3. But polling_mode is NEVER reset to 0 once it's set to 1 at line 912\n\nThis is the bug! Once polling_mode is set to 1 during error recovery, it stays at 1 even after successful command exchanges. This means:\n- The driver will stay in polling mode, polling the codec for every response instead of relying on interrupts\n- This is inefficient and can cause performance issues, especially after multiple suspend/resume cycles\n\nThe fix should be to reset polling_mode to 0 when coming out of suspend. The test might be provided later. Let me focus on identifying the buggy files and functions based on my analysis.\n\nBased on my thorough analysis of the code, I've identified the bug:\n\n**Root Cause**: When the HDA Intel controller encounters communication timeouts with the codec during normal operation, it enters fallback modes:\n1. Polling mode (polling_mode = 1)\n2. Single command mode (single_cmd = 1)\n\nHowever, these flags are never reset during the suspend/resume cycle. When the device is suspended and resumed, the chip and codec are properly reinitialized, but the fallback mode flags remain set from the previous error condition.\n\n**Why This Is a Bug**:\n- The polling_mode flag being stuck at 1 means all future codec communication will use polling instead of interrupt-driven responses\n- In polling mode, the driver has to continuously poll the codec status register instead of being notified by interrupts\n- After multiple suspend/resume cycles where errors occur, the driver becomes stuck in increasingly degraded modes\n- This explains the \"choppy\" audio with \"2 second silences\" - the driver is polling with delays\n\n**Buggy Location**:\n- File: `sound/pci/hda/hda_intel.c`\n- Function: `azx_resume()` - needs to reset polling_mode and poll_count\n- Alternatively: `azx_init_chip()` - could reset these flags when initializing\n\nThe fix is to reset polling_mode to 0 and poll_count to 0 in the azx_resume function after azx_init_chip is called. This allows the driver to attempt normal interrupt-based responses again after resume.\n\nLet me verify this is the correct file and write the
